Empirical Refutation of the Denial of Pain
Al-Nasafi presents empirical evidence and logical consequences to refute the denial of children's pain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the empirical arguments al-Nasafi uses to refute the denial of children's pain.

Core Idea
Children clearly show pain through crying, illness, and harm — proof that their pain is real.

Having introduced the shocking claim that children feel no pain, al-Nasafi now provides a series of observations anyone can verify. He argues from common experience, physical effects, and the absurd consequences of the denial. This lesson walks through his main arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the empirical observations
Read the passage noting the specific signs of joy, sadness, emaciation, and screaming that children exhibit.
2
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Al-Nasafi argues that if children felt no pain, harming them would not be sinful. Consider the logical consequence.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Appreciate the appeal to common sense and personal memory
Notice that al-Nasafi appeals to the ridicule of common people and personal recollection of pain from one's own childhood.
4
Conclude the obviousness of the refutation
Al-Nasafi ends by saying the belief is so obviously false it does not merit further time. Reflect on why this is so.
He states it is established by intuition (badaha) and primary cognitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اضطرت الحيرة لهم في هذه المسألة طائفة منهم إلى إنكار المشاهدة والخروج إلى التجاهل، فزعم أن الأطفال لا يتألمون ولو أن أوصالهم قطعت وجعلت أعضاؤهم إربا إربا لما تأملوا بذلك وهو قول بكر بن عبد ربه رئيس البكرية من أهل البدع وهو المعروف بابن أخت عبد الواحد بن زيد. وروى يحيى بن كامل البصري المعروف بالحجدري هذه المقابلة أيضا عن النجدات من الخوارج وهم أصحاب نجدة بن عامر الحنفي المعروف بنجدة الحروى أحد رؤساء الخوارج، وهذا من باب إنكار المشاهدة. فإنا نرى من الأطفال آثار السرور بالأسباب التي يسر أهلها، والحزن والبكاء لأجل أسباب الحزن، ونرى الهزال والضنا يظهر فيهم عند نزول مرض أو جراحة، ويسمع الصراخ والعويل عند ضربة أو صدمة حلت بهم، ثم لو كان الأمر على ما يزعمون لما أثم من ضرب صبيًا ضربا مبرحا أو جرحه جراحة مثخنة إذ لم يصر بذلك مضرابًا لصبي مرديًا له، ثم لو صورت هذه العقيدة لعوام الخليقة لقابلوا القائل بها بالهزء والسخرية، وحكموا عليه بالعناد والتجاهل، ثم كل عاقل يتذكر في نفسه آلاما ما لحقته في الأحوال التي هي قريبة من حالة الكلفة وتوجه المحنة عليه، وهذا لا معنى لتضييع الوقت بالاشتغال بما له من دلائل الإبطال لثبوت ذلك في البداهة وأوائل المعارف.
Then confusion forced a group among them in this matter to deny observation and to resort to feigned ignorance, so they claimed that children do not feel pain, even if their joints were cut and their limbs were made piece by piece, they would not perceive that. This is the statement of Bakr ibn 'Abd Rabbih, the head of the Bakriyya, a people of innovation, known as Ibn Ukht 'Abd al-Wahid ibn Zayd. And Yahya ibn Kamil al-Basri, known as al-Hajdari, also narrated this absurdity from the Najdat, a sect of the Kharijites, who are the followers of Najda ibn 'Amir al-Hanafi, known as Najda al-Haruri, one of the leaders of the Kharijites. This falls under the category of denying observation. For we see in children signs of joy due to causes that gladden their families, and sadness and crying due to causes of sorrow, and we see emaciation and thinness appear in them when illness or injury befalls them, and we hear screaming and wailing when a blow or shock occurs to them. Then if the matter were as they claim, no one would sin by severely beating a child or inflicting a serious wound, since by that he would not be harming the child or destroying him. Moreover, if this doctrine were presented to the common people, they would mock and ridicule the one who says it, and judge him to be obstinate and ignorant. Furthermore, every rational person recalls in himself pains that afflicted him in states close to a condition of hardship and trial. And it is pointless to waste time occupying oneself with something that has such obvious disproofs, since it is established by intuition and primary cognitions.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the extreme claim made by some sects (the Bakriyya and the Najdat) who denied that children feel pain, in order to avoid the implications of the doctrine of al-Aslah. Al-Nasafi begins by stating that confusion forced this group to deny observable reality and resort to willful ignorance. They claimed that even if children's limbs are cut, they do not feel pain. He identifies the proponent as Bakr ibn 'Abd Rabbih. Then he lists empirical evidence: we see children showing joy and sadness, we see physical effects like emaciation from illness, we hear screams of pain. He then argues that if pain were not real, then harming a child would not be sinful, which is absurd. He also notes that common sense would ridicule such a claim. Finally, he says every rational person recalls their own past pains. Therefore, this belief is so obviously false that it does not merit further time.

Key Terms
الأطفال
الألم
المشاهدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Since children cannot speak, their pain is not real.
Correction: Al-Nasafi points to visible signs like crying, emaciation, and screaming as evidence of real pain.

Checkpoint
What is one consequence al-Nasafi derives from the denial of children's pain?
A) It would make harming children permissible
B) It would make childhood easier
C) It would prove the existence of God
D) It would strengthen faith

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi refutes the denial of children's pain by appealing to observation, logic, common sense, and personal memory — showing the belief is self-evidently false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Recall a moment from your childhood when you experienced genuine pain or sorrow. How does that memory directly contradict the claim that children do not feel pain? Will you use that memory to strengthen your conviction in the truth taught by al-Nasafi?
?
If someone today told you that your child's cries are not a sign of real suffering, how would you respond using the evidence from this passage? Are you prepared to defend the reality of childhood pain against such denial?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that the denial of children's pain leads to moral absurdity, where harming a child is not sinful. In your own life, where do you see a tendency to downplay or dismiss the pain of others? What will you do today to take their suffering seriously?

Refutation of Denying Observable Effects on Children
Nasafi refutes the Khawarij denial of observable effects on children.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying observable causality in children leads to absurd moral consequences and how Nasafi uses empirical observation and common sense to refute this Khawarij position.

Core Idea
Observing children's reactions to joy and pain proves real causality.

Nasafi confronts an extreme Khawarij position that denies any observable causality in human actions. He uses children's clear responses to pleasure and injury as undeniable evidence that actions produce real effects. This passage shows how empirical observation combined with rational argument can refute even stubborn theological errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sect and their claim
Read the first sentence to learn which Khawarij subgroup is targeted and what they deny. This sets the stage for the refutation.
The sect is the followers of Najda ibn 'Amir.
2
Examine the empirical evidence
Notice the specific observable reactions Nasafi lists: joy/sadness, emaciation, shrieking. These are everyday observations that any rational person can verify.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Nasafi argues that if effects are denied, then harming a child would not be sinful. Reflect on why this consequence is absurd and morally untenable.
This is a logical consequence of the denial.
4
Consider the common sense reaction
Common people would mock such a belief. This appeal to universal intuition reinforces the argument.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Nasafi states that the matter is so obvious it needs no further proof; it is known by intuition and primary cognitions. This underscores the strength of the evidence.
This ties back to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من الخوارج وهم أصحاب نجدة بن عامر الحنفي المعروف بنجدة الحروى أحد رؤساء الخوارج، وهذا من باب إنكار المشاهدة. فإنا نرى من الأطفال آثار السرور بالأسباب التي يسر أهلها، والحزن والبكاء لأجل أسباب الحزن، ونرى الهزال والضنا يظهر فيهم عند نزول مرض أو جراحة، ويسمع الصراخ والعويل عند ضربة أو صدمة حلت بهم، ثم لو كان الأمر على ما يزعمون لما أثم من ضرب صبيًا ضربا مبرحا أو جرحه جراحة مثخنة إذ لم يصر بذلك مضرابًا لصبي مرديًا له، ثم لو صورت هذه العقيدة لعوام الخليقة لقابلوا القائل بها بالهزء والسخرية، وحكموا عليه بالعناد والتجاهل، ثم كل عاقل يتذكر في نفسه آلاما ما لحقته في الأحوال التي هي قريبة من حالة الكلفة وتوجه المحنة عليه، وهذا لا معنى لتضييع الوقت بالاشتغال بما له من دلائل الإبطال لثبوت ذلك في البداهة وأوائل المعارف.
From the Khawarij, and they are the followers of Najda ibn 'Amir al-Hanafi known as Najda al-Haruri, one of the leaders of the Khawarij. This is a case of denying observation. For we see in children signs of joy due to causes that gladden their families, and sadness and crying due to causes of sadness, and we see emaciation and thinness appearing in them at the occurrence of illness or injury, and shrieking and wailing are heard upon a blow or shock that befalls them. Then if the matter were as they claim, no sin would be incurred by one who strikes a child severely or wounds him grievously, since he would not thereby become an injurer or destroyer of the child. Then if this belief were presented to the common people, they would meet its proponent with mockery and ridicule, and would judge him to be stubborn and ignorant. Then every rational person recollects in himself pains that befell him in states close to the condition of burden and the direction of trial upon him. And there is no meaning in wasting time by occupying oneself with what has proofs of invalidation, given its establishment in intuition and primary cognitions.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Khawarij sect (followers of Najda ibn 'Amir) who denied observable causality or effects of actions on children. The author first identifies the group as denying observation. Then he provides empirical evidence: we see children experiencing joy or sadness due to external causes, and physical changes from illness or injury. He argues that if their denial were true, then harming a child would not be sinful because the harm would not be attributed to the agent. He further points out that common sense would mock such a belief. Finally, he states that this matter is so obvious that it is a waste of time to argue against it, as it is known by intuition and primary cognitions. The argument follows a reductio ad absurdum: if effects are denied, then moral responsibility disappears and common sense is violated.

Key Terms
الخوارج
إنكار المشاهدة
البداهة
أوائل المعارف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Actions have no real observable effects on children; all changes are directly from God without any causal mediation.
Correction: Nasafi shows that children clearly react to external causes (joy from happy events, pain from injury), and denying this leads to absurd moral consequences (no sin for harming).

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used by Nasafi to refute the Khawarij denial of observable effects on children?
A) Citing Quranic verses about divine will.
B) Using empirical observations and common sense.
C) Appealing to consensus of scholars.
D) Logical proof that God must be just.

Key Takeaway
Observing children's clear reactions to joy and pain demonstrates that actions produce real effects, making the denial of causality rationally indefensible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have witnessed children's joy and pain—do you recognize that these are not random but caused? How does ignoring this affect your understanding of God's justice?
?
The Khawarij insisted on a belief that contradicted observable reality. Can you identify any belief in your own life that you hold despite clear evidence against it?
?
When you see a child suffer, do you attribute the suffering to a real cause, or do you fall into the trap of denying the obvious? How does that shape your response?

The Mu'tazili Claim: God Compelled to Do the Best
Nasafi states the Mu'tazili doctrine that God is compelled to do the best and denies His generosity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah and why they argued that God is compelled to do what is best for His creatures, and the immediate consequence that God cannot be described as generous or bountiful.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila made God a debtor, not a gracious giver.

In this passage, Nasafi summarizes the core Mu'tazili position on divine action. According to them, God has no free choice but is obliged to do the most beneficial for His servants. This leads to a radical redefinition of God's attributes: He is not truly generous or bountiful, but merely fulfills a duty. Let's examine this claim and its first implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the doctrine
Read the Arabic statement carefully. Notice the key terms: لا مشيئة, مجبور, أصلح.
The Mu'tazila considered al-Aslah an obligation on God.
2
Identify the logical consequence
The claim that God is compelled leads to the conclusion that His actions are not gracious but obligatory. Find how Nasafi phrases this.
3
Reflect on the implication for God's attributes
If God's actions are merely fulfilling a right, He cannot be called generous or bountiful. This contradicts the Quranic verse cited.
The verse وَاللَّهُ ذُو الْفَضْلِ الْعَظِيمِ is used as evidence against the Mu'tazili view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم حاصل هذه المسألة عندهم أن الله تعالى لا مشيئة له في فعله ولا اختياره بل هو مجبور على أن يفعل ما هو أصلح لعباده، وليس له أن يفعل سوى ما فعل، وليس بمحسن ولا منفصل ولا مفضل ولا جواد، لأنه لم يفعل فعلاً إلا قضى به حقًا مستحقا عليه على وجه يصير بمنعه ظالمًا، ومن هذا وصف فعله لا يوصف بالإفضال والإحسان وأنه كاذب بقوله وَاللَّهُ ذُو الْفَضْلِ الْعَظِيمِ، وليس بمستوجب على أحد شكرًا ولا عبادة، إذ القاضي حق الغير لا يستوجب ذلك، وليس ممن يرغب إليه في طلب مرغوب أو إزالة مرهوب، إذ ليس له أن يفعل ذلك فإنه حيث أمر عباده بالرغبة إليه في ذلك أمرهم بالسخرية والهزء أو أمر بأن يطلب منه أن يتسفه أو يجوز عليهم ويظلم ، أو أمرهم أن يطلبوا منه أن لا يظلمهم بمنعهم حقهم المستحق، وأنه تعالى أحب أن يحمد بما لم يفعل من الإحسان والإفضال، وأمر أن يشكروه على ما لم يفعل إذ ليس شيء من فعله بإفضال وأنه عاجز عما به صلاح خلقه وغير قادر على دفع الفساد عن أحد، وأن قدرته انتهت إذ لم يقدر على أصلح مما فعل بكل أحد وأنه أنعم على إبليس وفرعون وهامان وأبي جهل وغيرهم من الكفرة حسب ما أنعم على جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين، وأنه ما اصطفى هؤلاء بشيء لم يصطف أولئك بمثله فكل كافر موفق معصوم منعم عليه مصطفى، وقد بينا في خلال كلامنا مجموع المعاني التي ذكرناها هذه عصمنا الله تعالى عن قول هذا عقباه.
Then the summary of this issue according to them is that Allah the Exalted has no will in His action nor choice, but He is compelled to do what is most beneficial (aslah) for His servants, and He cannot do other than what He did. And He is not a doer of good, nor a bestower, nor a giver of bounty, nor generous, because He never performed an action except that He fulfilled a right due upon Him in a way that by preventing it He would become unjust. And from this, His action is not described as bounty and beneficence, and that He is lying in His saying: 'And Allah is the possessor of great bounty' (Quran 2:105). And He is not deserving of gratitude or worship from anyone, since the one who fulfills the right of another does not deserve that. And He is not one to whom one turns in seeking a desired thing or removing a dreaded thing, since He is not able to do that. For when He commanded His servants to beseech Him in that matter, He commanded them to engage in mockery and ridicule, or He commanded them to ask Him to act foolishly or to oppress them, or He commanded them to ask Him not to oppress them by preventing their due right. And that the Exalted loved to be praised for what He did not do of beneficence and bounty, and commanded that they thank Him for what He did not do, since none of His actions is a bounty. And that He is incapable of what brings about the wellbeing of His creation, and unable to repel corruption from anyone, and that His power has ended, since He was not able to do what is more beneficial (aslah) than what He did for everyone. And that He bestowed favors upon Iblis, Pharaoh, Haman, Abu Jahl, and other disbelievers just as He bestowed favors upon all the prophets, messengers, and the angels brought near. And that He did not distinguish these by anything that He did not distinguish those by the like of it. So every disbeliever is successful, protected, favored, and chosen. And we have explained in the course of our speech the totality of the meanings that we have mentioned. May Allah protect us from uttering this, and its consequence.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah (the most beneficial) and its theological implications. The author summarizes the Mu'tazili position: God has no will or choice but is compelled to do the most beneficial for His creatures; He cannot do anything else. This leads to several consequences: God is not truly generous or beneficent, but only fulfills a duty; His actions cannot be described as bounty; He would be lying about His attribute of bounty; He is not owed gratitude; supplication becomes meaningless or even mocking; He is incapable of doing better; He treats believers and disbelievers equally; disbelievers would be considered favored. The author is clearly refuting this view, implying that such consequences are absurd and blasphemous. The passage ends with a prayer for protection from such beliefs.

Key Terms
الأصلح
المشيئة
الاختيار
المجبر
الإفضال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Mu'tazila affirmed God's will, but this passage shows their view of al-aslah denies God's free choice.
Correction: The Mu'tazila did not deny God's will entirely, but they held that God's will is determined by what is optimal, thus limiting His freedom. However, Nasafi presents it as a negation of will and choice.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazili doctrine summarized by Nasafi, why can God not be described as generous?
A) Because generosity requires giving beyond what is owed, but God only fulfills a duty.
B) Because God is too great to be described by human attributes.
C) Because generosity implies need, which God does not have.
D) Because the Quran does not call God generous.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah leads to the problematic consequence that God's actions are obligatory, not gracious, contradicting the Quranic description of His bounty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about God's actions in your life, do you ever secretly feel that He owes you something—health, provision, or relief from hardship? How does the Mu'tazili error of making God a debtor expose an ungrateful attitude in your own heart? Will you today repent of any entitlement and acknowledge that every blessing is pure, unearned generosity?
?
If God were compelled to give you what is 'best' for you, would you truly be grateful or would you take it for granted? Reflect: Have you ever thanked God not just for what you like, but for the very fact that He is free to give or withhold? How can you cultivate a heart that thanks Him not for outcomes, but for His voluntary grace?
?
The Mu'tazila made God's actions into duties. Do you treat your relationship with God as a transaction—obeying to get rewards, praying to get answers—rather than a relationship with a Generous Lord who gives out of His bounty? What is one concrete way you can respond to His grace today, not because you must, but because He is 'Dhul-Fadl al-'Azeem'?

Consequences for Worship and Supplication
Nasafi derives consequences about gratitude and supplication from Mu'tazili premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili implications that God does not deserve gratitude and that supplication becomes meaningless or mocking.

Core Idea
If God only does what He must, worship and supplication lose their meaning.

Nasafi continues to unfold the consequences of the Mu'tazili doctrine. If God is merely fulfilling a duty, then He is not owed gratitude, and turning to Him in prayer becomes absurd—either mocking or requesting injustice. Let's examine these deeply troubling conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Read the consequences
Read the passage about gratitude and supplication. Note how Nasafi logically derives these absurdities.
2
Analyze the logic on gratitude
If God only gives what is due, then He does not deserve thanks. This overturns the basis of worship.
3
Analyze the logic on supplication
Supplication implies asking for something beyond what is required. But if God cannot do anything but the best, then asking for something else is asking for injustice or foolishness.
Nasafi gives three possibilities: mockery, asking for foolishness, or asking not to be oppressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم حاصل هذه المسألة عندهم أن الله تعالى لا مشيئة له في فعله ولا اختياره بل هو مجبور على أن يفعل ما هو أصلح لعباده، وليس له أن يفعل سوى ما فعل، وليس بمحسن ولا منفصل ولا مفضل ولا جواد، لأنه لم يفعل فعلاً إلا قضى به حقًا مستحقا عليه على وجه يصير بمنعه ظالمًا، ومن هذا وصف فعله لا يوصف بالإفضال والإحسان وأنه كاذب بقوله وَاللَّهُ ذُو الْفَضْلِ الْعَظِيمِ، وليس بمستوجب على أحد شكرًا ولا عبادة، إذ القاضي حق الغير لا يستوجب ذلك، وليس ممن يرغب إليه في طلب مرغوب أو إزالة مرهوب، إذ ليس له أن يفعل ذلك فإنه حيث أمر عباده بالرغبة إليه في ذلك أمرهم بالسخرية والهزء أو أمر بأن يطلب منه أن يتسفه أو يجوز عليهم ويظلم ، أو أمرهم أن يطلبوا منه أن لا يظلمهم بمنعهم حقهم المستحق، وأنه تعالى أحب أن يحمد بما لم يفعل من الإحسان والإفضال، وأمر أن يشكروه على ما لم يفعل إذ ليس شيء من فعله بإفضال وأنه عاجز عما به صلاح خلقه وغير قادر على دفع الفساد عن أحد، وأن قدرته انتهت إذ لم يقدر على أصلح مما فعل بكل أحد وأنه أنعم على إبليس وفرعون وهامان وأبي جهل وغيرهم من الكفرة حسب ما أنعم على جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين، وأنه ما اصطفى هؤلاء بشيء لم يصطف أولئك بمثله فكل كافر موفق معصوم منعم عليه مصطفى، وقد بينا في خلال كلامنا مجموع المعاني التي ذكرناها هذه عصمنا الله تعالى عن قول هذا عقباه.

This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah (the most beneficial) and its theological implications. The author summarizes the Mu'tazili position: God has no will or choice but is compelled to do the most beneficial for His creatures; He cannot do anything else. This leads to several consequences: God is not truly generous or beneficent, but only fulfills a duty; His actions cannot be described as bounty; He would be lying about His attribute of bounty; He is not owed gratitude; supplication becomes meaningless or even mocking; He is incapable of doing better; He treats believers and disbelievers equally; disbelievers would be considered favored. The author is clearly refuting this view, implying that such consequences are absurd and blasphemous. The passage ends with a prayer for protection from such beliefs.

Key Terms
شكر
عبادة
رغبة
هزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, why does the Mu'tazili view make supplication problematic?
A) Because God is too busy to answer prayers.
B) Because God is compelled to do only the best, so asking for anything else is asking for injustice or futility.
C) Because supplication is not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because the Mu'tazila reject all forms of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili position reduces worship to an empty form and supplication to an absurdity, as God would only be fulfilling duties.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you make du'a, do you truly believe that God can change your situation, or do you sometimes feel it is just a formality? This lesson says that if God were compelled, supplication would be mockery. How does that truth renew your conviction that your du'a reaches a free and willing Lord?
?
Think of a time you thanked God for something you felt you deserved. In light of this passage, how does that cheapen gratitude? What must you change in your heart so that your shukr and 'ibadah are genuine responses to grace, not expectations of duty?

Consequences for Divine Power and Justice
Nasafi concludes by stating further absurd consequences about God's power and justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah leads to the absurd conclusion that God is incapable, treats believers and disbelievers equally, and is hypocritical.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazili view makes God weak, unjust, and insincere.

Nasafi continues to reveal the devastating consequences of the doctrine. It implies that God cannot do better, that His power is limited, and that He favors believers and disbelievers equally, stripping the distinction of any meaning. He ends with a prayer for protection from such beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the final consequences
Read the passage about incapability, equality of treatment, and the claim that God praises Himself for what He did not do.
2
Analyze the claim of incapability
If God must do the best, then He could not have done a better act, implying His power is limited.
3
Analyze the equality of believers and disbelievers
If God's favor is only fulfilling duty, then He favors all equally, making prophetic distinctions meaningless.
Nasafi lists disbelievers like Iblis and Pharaoh as being equally favored.
4
Reflect on the author's prayer
Nasafi ends with a supplication for protection, showing the grave danger of this doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم حاصل هذه المسألة عندهم أن الله تعالى لا مشيئة له في فعله ولا اختياره بل هو مجبور على أن يفعل ما هو أصلح لعباده، وليس له أن يفعل سوى ما فعل، وليس بمحسن ولا منفصل ولا مفضل ولا جواد، لأنه لم يفعل فعلاً إلا قضى به حقًا مستحقا عليه على وجه يصير بمنعه ظالمًا، ومن هذا وصف فعله لا يوصف بالإفضال والإحسان وأنه كاذب بقوله وَاللَّهُ ذُو الْفَضْلِ الْعَظِيمِ، وليس بمستوجب على أحد شكرًا ولا عبادة، إذ القاضي حق الغير لا يستوجب ذلك، وليس ممن يرغب إليه في طلب مرغوب أو إزالة مرهوب، إذ ليس له أن يفعل ذلك فإنه حيث أمر عباده بالرغبة إليه في ذلك أمرهم بالسخرية والهزء أو أمر بأن يطلب منه أن يتسفه أو يجوز عليهم ويظلم ، أو أمرهم أن يطلبوا منه أن لا يظلمهم بمنعهم حقهم المستحق، وأنه تعالى أحب أن يحمد بما لم يفعل من الإحسان والإفضال، وأمر أن يشكروه على ما لم يفعل إذ ليس شيء من فعله بإفضال وأنه عاجز عما به صلاح خلقه وغير قادر على دفع الفساد عن أحد، وأن قدرته انتهت إذ لم يقدر على أصلح مما فعل بكل أحد وأنه أنعم على إبليس وفرعون وهامان وأبي جهل وغيرهم من الكفرة حسب ما أنعم على جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين، وأنه ما اصطفى هؤلاء بشيء لم يصطف أولئك بمثله فكل كافر موفق معصوم منعم عليه مصطفى، وقد بينا في خلال كلامنا مجموع المعاني التي ذكرناها هذه عصمنا الله تعالى عن قول هذا عقباه.
Then the summary of this issue according to them is that Allah the Exalted has no will in His action nor choice, but He is compelled to do what is most beneficial (aslah) for His servants, and He cannot do other than what He did. And He is not a doer of good, nor a bestower, nor a giver of bounty, nor generous, because He never performed an action except that He fulfilled a right due upon Him in a way that by preventing it He would become unjust. And from this, His action is not described as bounty and beneficence, and that He is lying in His saying: 'And Allah is the possessor of great bounty' (Quran 2:105). And He is not deserving of gratitude or worship from anyone, since the one who fulfills the right of another does not deserve that. And He is not one to whom one turns in seeking a desired thing or removing a dreaded thing, since He is not able to do that. For when He commanded His servants to beseech Him in that matter, He commanded them to engage in mockery and ridicule, or He commanded them to ask Him to act foolishly or to oppress them, or He commanded them to ask Him not to oppress them by preventing their due right. And that the Exalted loved to be praised for what He did not do of beneficence and bounty, and commanded that they thank Him for what He did not do, since none of His actions is a bounty. And that He is incapable of what brings about the wellbeing of His creation, and unable to repel corruption from anyone, and that His power has ended, since He was not able to do what is more beneficial (aslah) than what He did for everyone. And that He bestowed favors upon Iblis, Pharaoh, Haman, Abu Jahl, and other disbelievers just as He bestowed favors upon all the prophets, messengers, and the angels brought near. And that He did not distinguish these by anything that He did not distinguish those by the like of it. So every disbeliever is successful, protected, favored, and chosen. And we have explained in the course of our speech the totality of the meanings that we have mentioned. May Allah protect us from uttering this, and its consequence.

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-Aslah (the most beneficial) and its theological implications. The author summarizes the Mu'tazili position: God has no will or choice but is compelled to do the most beneficial for His creatures; He cannot do anything else. The author is clearly refuting this view, implying that such consequences are absurd and blasphemous. The passage ends with a prayer for protection from such beliefs.

Authenticity of the Hadith on Qadariyya
Nasafi affirms the authentic transmission of the hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi asserts the authenticity of the hadith labeling the Qadariyya as the Magians of this ummah, and why its transmission is considered undeniable.

Core Idea
The hadith against Qadariyya is so widely transmitted that no sect can reject it.

Before examining the theological claims of the Qadariyya, Nasafi first establishes the authority of a prophetic hadith that condemns their position. By demonstrating that this hadith has been transmitted through widespread, reliable chains, he removes any doubt about its authenticity. This passage shows how hadith criticism is used to ground theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice the key terms: استفاضة, جرح وتعديل, طبقات.
2
Identify the main claim
What does Nasafi assert about the hadith? He asserts it is authentically established via widespread transmission (istifada).
3
Understand why it is undeniable
Nasafi says no sect could reject it because it is well-known among hadith critics who specialized in authenticity and narrator criticism.
This shows the hadith's authority is not sectarian but based on scholarly consensus.
4
Connect to hadith sciences
Identify the terms related to hadith criticism: jarh wa ta'dil, knowledge of dates, knowledge of strata. Reflect on how these give the hadith its strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في القدرية: صح المروي عن النبي له على طريق الاستفاضة القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة صحة لم يجد أحد من فرق الأمة سبيلاً إلى دفعه، لاشتهاره في النقلة الذين تجردوا لنقد الأحاديث والتمييز بين صحيحها وسقيمها وثابتها ومردودها، واشتهروا بصناعة الجرح والتعديل ومعرفة التواريخ والعلم بالطبقات والتفرقة بين الثقات من غيرهم.
Discussion of the Qadariyya: The narration from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is authentically established via widespread transmission (istifada): 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah.' A authenticity such that no one from the sects of the ummah found a way to reject it, due to its widespread fame among the transmitters who devoted themselves to criticizing hadiths and distinguishing between their authentic and weak, established and rejected [reports], and who were famous for the science of jarh wa ta'dil, knowledge of dates, knowledge of strata, and differentiation between reliable and unreliable [transmitters].
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the authenticity of a well-known hadith that labels the Qadariyya (those who deny divine predestination) as the Magians (Zoroastrians) of this ummah. The author states that this hadith is authentically transmitted via istifada (widespread transmission that yields certainty). He emphasizes that no sect has been able to reject it because it is well-known among the hadith critics who specialized in analyzing and authenticating hadiths, and who are experts in jarh wa ta'dil (criticism of narrators), historical knowledge, and classification of narrators by strata. The author uses this to show the gravity of the Qadariyya position.

القدرية
الاستفاضة
مجوس هذه الأمة
الجرح والتعديل
الطبقات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the hadith is weak or disputed, with no universal acceptance.
Correction: Nasafi asserts that the hadith is authentically established via widespread transmission (istifada) and that no sect has been able to reject it due to its fame among hadith critics.

Checkpoint

C) It is a fabricated hadith.
D) It is only accepted by one sect.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi establishes the foundational authenticity of the hadith against the Qadariyya through its widespread transmission and acceptance among hadith scholars.

The Prophetic Identification of the Qadariyya
Authenticity of the hadith and its universal application to Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith 'Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' is authenticated and why it was applied to the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The Prophet's hadith about Qadariyya is universally accepted, and all sects agree it refers to the Mu'tazila.

This lesson examines the foundational hadith that identifies the Qadariyya as the Magians of the Muslim community. We will see how its authenticity is established through widespread transmission and how the early community understood it as a reference to the Mu'tazila, despite the Mu'tazila's vehement rejection of that label.

Guided Path
1
Trace the authenticity of the hadith
Read how the author establishes the hadith's irrefutable status through the science of hadith criticism.
2
Understand the universal application
Notice that all sects initially agreed that the hadith refers to the Mu'tazila.
3
Observe the Mu'tazila's reaction
See how the Mu'tazila refused the name and even preferred being called heretics over being called Qadariyya.
This shows the stigma attached to the term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في القدرية:
صح المروي عن النبي على طريق الاستفاضة القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة صحة لم يجد أحد من فرق الأمة سبيلاً إلى دفعه، لاشتهاره في النقلة الذين تجردوا لنقد الأحاديث والتمييز بين صحيحها وسقيمها وثابتها ومردودها، واشتهروا بصناعة الجرح والتعديل ومعرفة التواريخ والعلم بالطبقات والتفرقة بين الثقات من الرواة والضعفاء منهم وتلقيبهم إياه بالقبول والشهادة له بالصدق والثبوت عن الصادق المصدق، ثم إن جميع فرق الأمة صرفوه إلى المعتزلة، وتبرأت المعتزلة عن الاسم وأبوا قبوله على وجه كانت التسمية بالزندقة والإلحاد عليهم أهون وأيسر من هذه التسمية، ثم زعموا أن ذلك مصروف إلى من يقول القدر خيره وشره من الله بدلالة حديث آخر روى عنه عليه السلام وهو أنه قال: "القدرية خصماء الله" ووجه دلالته أن خصم الله من يضيف ما قبح من فعله إليه ويقول إن الله تعالى هو الذي أراده وأوجده، لا من ينزهه عن القبائح والشرور، قالوا: والاتفاق في المقالة يدل على ذلك فإن المجوس يقولون : نكاح الأمهات والأخوات ووطئهن بإرادة الله تعالى، وكذا أنتم تقولون هكذا، قالوا فأما نحن نقول: ليس شيء من ذلك بإرادة الله تعالى، وقالوا: نحن ننفي القدر فنقول: الله تعالى لا يقدر الشرور والمعاصي وخصومنا يثبتون ذلك والاسم المأخوذ عن معنى يضاف إلى مثبته دون نافيه.
وأما أهل الحق فإنهم قالوا: إن القدرية هم المعتزلة فإنه عليه السلام قال: "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة" ووجه الكشف عن المراد بهذا اللفظ والمسمى بهذا الاسم هو النظر في المقالات ليظهر أن المخالف للمجوس أي فريق والموافق فيما هو من خاصية مذاهبهم من هو، ولا وجه لذلك غير هذا.
The discussion on the Qadariyya: The narration from the Prophet, peace be upon him, via widespread transmission that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation is established with such authenticity that none of the sects of the nation found a way to reject it, due to its fame among the transmitters who devoted themselves to critiquing hadiths and distinguishing between their authentic and weak, established and rejected, and became renowned in the craft of jarh and ta'dil, knowledge of histories, knowledge of classes, and differentiation between reliable narrators and weak ones among them, and their labeling it with acceptance and testimony to its truth and confirmation from the truthful and confirmed. Then all sects of the nation interpreted it as referring to the Mu'tazila, and the Mu'tazila disassociated themselves from the name and refused to accept it to the extent that being called Zindiq and heretic was easier and lighter for them than this designation. Then they claimed that it refers to those who say that destiny, its good and evil, is from God, based on another hadith narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he said: 'The Qadariyya are the adversaries of God.' And the indication of that is that the adversary of God is one who attributes what is ugly from His action to Him and says that God, exalted, intended it and brought it into existence, not one who declares Him transcendent of ugly things and evils. They said: And agreement in doctrine indicates that, for the Magians say: Marriage to mothers and sisters and their intercourse is by the will of God, and likewise you say this. They said: As for us, we say: None of that is by the will of God. And they said: We negate destiny and say: God, exalted, does not have power over evils and sins, and our opponents affirm that, and the name derived from the meaning is attributed to its affirmer, not its negator. As for Ahl al-Haqq, they said: The Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila, for he, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' And the way of uncovering what is intended by this expression and the one named by this name is to examine the doctrines to make clear which faction opposes the Magians and which agrees with them in what is specific to their doctrines, and there is no way other than this.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the orthodox position on the identity of the Qadariyya. It begins by establishing the authenticity of the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' through widespread transmission (tawatur), noting that no sect can deny it due to its impeccable chain. Then it explains that all sects initially interpreted this as referring to the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazila, however, rejected this label, preferring even the charge of heresy (zandaqa) over being called Qadariyya. They attempted to reinterpret the hadith by citing another hadith that 'the Qadariyya are the adversaries of God,' arguing that it applies to those who affirm destiny (i.e., Ahl al-Sunna) because they attribute evil to God. They draw a parallel with the Magians who attribute sinful acts like incest to God's will. The Mu'tazila claim that they themselves negate destiny (i.e., deny God creates evil) and therefore the name should apply only to those who affirm it. Finally, Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) respond by affirming that the Qadariyya are indeed the Mu'tazila, because the proper method to identify them is to examine doctrines: the Mu'tazila, by denying God's creation of all acts, align with the Magian denial of God's universal will, while Ahl al-Sunna oppose that. Thus, the prophetic identification stands.

Key Terms
القدرية
المعتزلة
مجوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith is weak or not universally accepted.
Correction: The author shows it is sahih via tawatur and no sect can reject it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the hadith 'Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah' characterized?
A) It is a weak hadith that few accept.
B) It is established via widespread transmission and cannot be rejected.
C) It is only accepted by the Mu'tazila.
D) It is rejected by all sects.

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' is authentic and was universally understood to refer to the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Mu'tazila found being called Zindiq easier than being called Qadariyya, what label or truth about yourself do you find hardest to accept? Are you willing to accept it even if it costs you your reputation?
?
The hadith critics worked tirelessly to authenticate this hadith. Do you treat the words of the Prophet with that level of reverence, or do you dismiss teachings that challenge your worldview?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected the label because they thought it was false. Is there an area where you are rejecting a truth because it doesn't fit your self-image? What would it take for you to submit to it?

The Mu'tazila's Counterargument and the Response of Ahl al-Haqq
Mu'tazila's reinterpretation and Ahl al-Haqq's refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila's attempt to reinterpret the hadith and how Ahl al-Haqq refuted them.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila used a second hadith to deflect the label, but Ahl al-Haqq showed they are truly the Qadariyya by comparing doctrines.

After the Mu'tazila rejected being called Qadariyya, they offered an alternative interpretation based on another hadith. They claimed that the term actually applies to those who affirm that all acts, including evil, are from God—i.e., Ahl al-Sunna. This lesson examines their reasoning and the decisive response from Ahl al-Haqq, who demonstrated that the Mu'tazila's own doctrines align with Magian beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila's argument
They cite a hadith about Qadariyya being adversaries of God and argue it targets those who attribute evil to God.
2
Analyze their parallel with Magians
They compare Ahl al-Sunna's belief in God's will for all things to the Magians' justification of incest.
This is a polemical tactic.
3
See the response of Ahl al-Haqq
Ahl al-Haqq assert that the proper method is to compare doctrines: Mu'tazila deny God's power over evil, aligning with Magians, so they are the Qadariyya.
They turn the tables.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في القدرية:
صح المروي عن النبي على طريق الاستفاضة القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة صحة لم يجد أحد من فرق الأمة سبيلاً إلى دفعه، لاشتهاره في النقلة الذين تجردوا لنقد الأحاديث والتمييز بين صحيحها وسقيمها وثابتها ومردودها، واشتهروا بصناعة الجرح والتعديل ومعرفة التواريخ والعلم بالطبقات والتفرقة بين الثقات من الرواة والضعفاء منهم وتلقيبهم إياه بالقبول والشهادة له بالصدق والثبوت عن الصادق المصدق، ثم إن جميع فرق الأمة صرفوه إلى المعتزلة، وتبرأت المعتزلة عن الاسم وأبوا قبوله على وجه كانت التسمية بالزندقة والإلحاد عليهم أهون وأيسر من هذه التسمية، ثم زعموا أن ذلك مصروف إلى من يقول القدر خيره وشره من الله بدلالة حديث آخر روى عنه عليه السلام وهو أنه قال: "القدرية خصماء الله" ووجه دلالته أن خصم الله من يضيف ما قبح من فعله إليه ويقول إن الله تعالى هو الذي أراده وأوجده، لا من ينزهه عن القبائح والشرور، قالوا: والاتفاق في المقالة يدل على ذلك فإن المجوس يقولون : نكاح الأمهات والأخوات ووطئهن بإرادة الله تعالى، وكذا أنتم تقولون هكذا، قالوا فأما نحن نقول: ليس شيء من ذلك بإرادة الله تعالى، وقالوا: نحن ننفي القدر فنقول: الله تعالى لا يقدر الشرور والمعاصي وخصومنا يثبتون ذلك والاسم المأخوذ عن معنى يضاف إلى مثبته دون نافيه.
وأما أهل الحق فإنهم قالوا: إن القدرية هم المعتزلة فإنه عليه السلام قال: "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة" ووجه الكشف عن المراد بهذا اللفظ والمسمى بهذا الاسم هو النظر في المقالات ليظهر أن المخالف للمجوس أي فريق والموافق فيما هو من خاصية مذاهبهم من هو، ولا وجه لذلك غير هذا.
The discussion on the Qadariyya: The narration from the Prophet, peace be upon him, via widespread transmission that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation is established with such authenticity that none of the sects of the nation found a way to reject it, due to its fame among the transmitters who devoted themselves to critiquing hadiths and distinguishing between their authentic and weak, established and rejected, and became renowned in the craft of jarh and ta'dil, knowledge of histories, knowledge of classes, and differentiation between reliable narrators and weak ones among them, and their labeling it with acceptance and testimony to its truth and confirmation from the truthful and confirmed. Then all sects of the nation interpreted it as referring to the Mu'tazila, and the Mu'tazila disassociated themselves from the name and refused to accept it to the extent that being called Zindiq and heretic was easier and lighter for them than this designation. Then they claimed that it refers to those who say that destiny, its good and evil, is from God, based on another hadith narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he said: 'The Qadariyya are the adversaries of God.' And the indication of that is that the adversary of God is one who attributes what is ugly from His action to Him and says that God, exalted, intended it and brought it into existence, not one who declares Him transcendent of ugly things and evils. They said: And agreement in doctrine indicates that, for the Magians say: Marriage to mothers and sisters and their intercourse is by the will of God, and likewise you say this. They said: As for us, we say: None of that is by the will of God. And they said: We negate destiny and say: God, exalted, does not have power over evils and sins, and our opponents affirm that, and the name derived from the meaning is attributed to its affirmer, not its negator. As for Ahl al-Haqq, they said: The Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila, for he, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation.' And the way of uncovering what is intended by this expression and the one named by this name is to examine the doctrines to make clear which faction opposes the Magians and which agrees with them in what is specific to their doctrines, and there is no way other than this.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage defines and defends the orthodox position on the identity of the Qadariyya. It begins by establishing the authenticity of the hadith 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this nation' through widespread transmission (tawatur), noting that no sect can deny it due to its impeccable chain. Then it explains that all sects initially interpreted this as referring to the Mu'tazila. The Mu'tazila, however, rejected this label, preferring even the charge of heresy (zandaqa) over being called Qadariyya. They attempted to reinterpret the hadith by citing another hadith that 'the Qadariyya are the adversaries of God,' arguing that it applies to those who affirm destiny (i.e., Ahl al-Sunna) because they attribute evil to God. They draw a parallel with the Magians who attribute sinful acts like incest to God's will. The Mu'tazila claim that they themselves negate destiny (i.e., deny God creates evil) and therefore the name should apply only to those who affirm it. Finally, Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) respond by affirming that the Qadariyya are indeed the Mu'tazila, because the proper method to identify them is to examine doctrines: the Mu'tazila, by denying God's creation of all acts, align with the Magian denial of God's universal will, while Ahl al-Sunna oppose that. Thus, the prophetic identification stands.

Key Terms
القدرية
المعتزلة
مجوس
خصماء الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People think Qadariyya means those who believe in free will (like Mu'tazila), but actually the hadith identifies them as those who deny God's creation of acts.
Correction: The passage shows that the Qadariyya are those who negate destiny (i.e., deny God creates evil), which is the Mu'tazila position.

Checkpoint
What method does Ahl al-Haqq use to identify the true Qadariyya?
A) They rely solely on the chain of narration.
B) They examine the doctrines of each group to see who aligns with the Magians.
C) They accept the Mu'tazila's own interpretation.
D) They reject both hadiths as inauthentic.

Key Takeaway
By comparing doctrines, Ahl al-Haqq demonstrated that the Mu'tazila, not Ahl al-Sunna, are the Qadariyya condemned in the hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accuse others of being misguided, do you first examine your own heart for the same faults? The Mu'tazila called Ahl al-Sunna Qadariyya while themselves being the true ones. In what area of your life are you projecting your own shortcomings onto others? Write down one specific instance and commit to self-examination before blame.
?
Are you willing to compare your beliefs with the clear teachings of the Salaf, even if it means admitting you align with a group you condemn? This lesson shows the danger of relying on labels. Ask yourself: what doctrine do you hold that might actually mirror those you criticize? Be honest.
?
The Mu'tazila twisted a hadith to deflect blame. Have you ever used a religious text or argument to avoid admitting a fault or to justify a wrong action? Reflect on a recent situation and commit to truth over comfort.

The Qadariyya Controversy: Mu'tazila or Their Opponents?
Controversy over the identification of Qadariyya resolved by Ahl al-Haqq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ahl al-Haqq identify the Qadariyya as the Mu'tazila based on a hadith and doctrinal analysis, and how the Mu'tazila attempted to redirect the name.

Core Idea
The name Qadariyya attaches by doctrine, not etymology.

This passage presents a key sectarian debate: who are the Qadariyya? The Mu'tazila reject the label and claim it belongs to those who affirm divine decree. Ahl al-Haqq respond by citing a hadith and comparing doctrines to show that the Mu'tazila are the true inheritors of the label. In this lesson, we'll trace the argument and understand the method of doctrinal comparison.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice the back-and-forth structure: first the Mu'tazila reject the name, then they try to shift it to their opponents.
The passage uses two hadiths as evidence.
2
Identify the two hadiths
Find the hadith cited by the Mu'tazila (Qadariyya are adversaries of God) and the one cited by Ahl al-Haqq (Qadariyya are Magians of this community). Understand how each side interprets them.
The second hadith is key for Ahl al-Haqq.
3
Understand the doctrinal comparison
See how the passage argues that the name should go to those who share doctrine with the Magians. The Mu'tazila deny divine decree of evil, aligning with the Magians, while their opponents affirm it.
This is the core of Ahl al-Haqq's argument.
4
Conclude with Ahl al-Haqq's position
The passage ends with the Ahl al-Haqq's conclusion: Qadariyya = Mu'tazila, established by hadith and doctrinal analysis.
The name is not about linguistic derivation but theological affinity.

ثم إن جميع فرق الأمة صرفوه إلى المعتزلة، وتبرأت المعتزلة عن الاسم وأبوا قبوله على وجه كانت التسمية بالزندقة والإلحاد عليهم أهون وأيسر من هذه التسمية، ثم زعموا أن ذلك مصروف إلى من يقول القدر خيره وشره من الله بدلالة حديث آخر روى عنه عليه السلام وهو أنه قال: "القدرية خصماء الله". ووجه دلالته أن خصم الله من يضيف ما قبح من فعله إليه ويقول إن الله تعالى هو الذي أراده وأوجده، لا من ينزهه عن القبائح والشرور، قالوا: والاتفاق في المقالة يدل على ذلك فإن المجوس يقولون: نكاح الأمهات والأخوات ووطئهن بإرادة الله تعالى، وكذا أنتم تقولون هكذا، قالوا فأما نحن نقول: ليس شيء من ذلك بإرادة الله تعالى، وقالوا: نحن ننفي القدر فنقول: الله تعالى لا يقدر الشرور والمعاصي وخصومنا يثبتون ذلك والاسم المأخوذ عن معنى يضاف إلى مثبته دون نافيه. القدرية هم المعتزلة. وأما أهل الحق فإنهم قالوا: إن القدرية هم المعتزلة فإنه عليه السلام قال: "القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة". ووجه الكشف عن المراد بهذا اللفظ والمسمى بهذا الاسم هو النظر في المقالات ليظهر أن المخالف للمجوس أي فريق والموافق فيما هو من خاصية مذاهبهم من هو، ولا وجه لذلك غير هذا.
Then all sects of the community directed it (the name) to the Mu'tazila, and the Mu'tazila disassociated themselves from the name and refused to accept it to the extent that being called by the name of zandaqah (heresy) and ilhad (apostasy) was easier and lighter for them than this name. Then they claimed that it is directed to the one who says that decree (al-qadr), its good and evil, is from God, by the indication of another hadith narrated from him, peace be upon him, that he said: 'The Qadariyya are the adversaries of God.' And the aspect of its indication is that the adversary of God is the one who attributes what is ugly from his action to Him and says that God Almighty is the one who willed it and brought it into existence, not the one who declares Him transcendent of ugly things and evils. They said: And agreement in doctrine indicates that, for the Magians say: Marriage of mothers, sisters, and intercourse with them is by the will of God Almighty, and likewise you say so. They said: As for us, we say: Nothing of that is by the will of God Almighty. And they said: We deny al-qadr and say: God Almighty does not decree evils and sins, while our opponents affirm that, and the name derived from a meaning is attached to its affirmer, not its denier. Al-Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila. And as for the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq), they said: Indeed, the Qadariyya are the Mu'tazila, for he, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' And the way of uncovering the intended meaning of this utterance and the one named by this name is to examine the doctrines, so that it becomes apparent which faction opposes the Magians and which agrees with them in what is characteristic of their doctrines, and there is no way for that other than this.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument that first recounts how the Mu'tazila rejected the name 'Qadariyya' and attempted to redirect it to their opponents (those who affirm that all good and evil are from God), citing a hadith that the Qadariyya are 'adversaries of God' because they attribute evil to Him. The author then shows the Ahl al-Haqq's position: they insist that the Qadariyya are indeed the Mu'tazila, based on another hadith that calls them 'the Magians of this community'. The method for determining the correct referent is not merely textual but involves comparing doctrines to see which party shares core tenets with the Magians. The Mu'tazila's own argument that the name should attach to those who affirm divine decree (their opponents) is turned against them: the Ahl al-Haqq use the second hadith and doctrinal analysis to fix the name on the Mu'tazila. The key point is that the name is defined by doctrinal affinity, not by literal etymology of the root qadara.

Key Terms
القدرية (al-Qadariyya)
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazila)
المجوس (al-Majus/Magians)
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq/People of Truth)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya are those who affirm that all good and evil are from God.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Haqq, the Qadariyya are actually the Mu'tazila, who deny divine decree of evil. This is shown by the hadith calling them Magians and doctrinal comparison.

Checkpoint
According to Ahl al-Haqq in this passage, what is the primary basis for identifying the Qadariyya as the Mu'tazila?
A) A hadith that the Qadariyya are adversaries of God.
B) A hadith that the Qadariyya are the Magians of this community, combined with doctrinal comparison.
C) The Mu'tazila's own claim that the name should go to those who affirm divine decree.
D) The fact that the Mu'tazila deny divine decree.

Key Takeaway
The identity of the Qadariyya is determined not by linguistic derivation but by doctrinal affinity, leading Ahl al-Haqq to identify them with the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever cling to a religious label or name more than to the truth it represents? This passage shows that even a term like 'Qadariyya' was fiercely disputed. Is there a label you own that keeps you from humbly examining your own beliefs?
?
When you hear a criticism of another Muslim group, do you immediately accept or reject it based on your own affiliation, or do you, like the Ahl al-Haqq, actually compare doctrines to see where the real alignment lies? What would it take for you to practice this method with sincerity?
?
The Mu'tazila found being called Qadariyya worse than being called heretics. What does that reveal about the power of names in your own heart? Is there a name or reputation you protect so fiercely that it blinds you to the truth about yourself or others?

The Mu'tazila and Magians: A Shared Doctrine of Two Creators
Detailed evidence that Mu'tazila share Magian belief in two creators of good and evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila's doctrine of the occurrence of God's will without His choice parallels the Magian belief in a wicked thought that produced a second creator of evil, thus undermining God's absolute sovereignty.

Core Idea
Both Mu'tazila and Magians posit a secondary principle that limits God's exclusive creative power.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla reveals a startling doctrinal kinship. The author argues that the Mu'tazila, despite their apparent monotheism, share the Magian (Zoroastrian) belief in two sources of creation—one for good and one for evil. By examining this parallel, we see why the Mu'tazila are counted among the Qadariyya. Let us explore the evidence step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its argument. Then read the translation to understand the flow.
2
Identify the Magian belief
The author summarizes the Magian view: God alone, then a wicked thought arose, producing Iblis who creates evil. Note that this thought occurs without God's direct control.
This is the key parallel.
3
Identify the Mu'tazila parallel
Find where the author shows that the Mu'tazila say God's will occurred without His choice, bringing about all the world. See how this mirrors the Magian thought.
4
Why does the name difference not matter?
The author dismisses the difference in terminology (thought vs. will) because the meaning is the same: an occurrence not fully under God's control.
This is crucial for understanding the critique.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider what it means for the Mu'tazila to be identified with the Qadariyya. Why does this parallel undermine their claim of strict tawhid?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من عرف المذاهب ووقف على ما لفرق الأمة من المقالات عرف أن المعتزلة هم المخصوصون من فرق الأمة بمشاركة المجوس فيما هو من خصائص مذاهبهم. وبيان ذلك أن المجوس قالوا كان الله تعالى واحدا لا شريك له، ثم حدثت منه فكرة رديئة على ما حكينا قبل هذا من مقالتهم، فحدث إبليس عليه اللعنة من تلك الفكرة الرديئة فخلق هو الشرور في العالم، والله تعالى خلق الخيرات من غير أن كان الله قدرة على خلق شيء من الشر والفساد أو لإبليس قدرة على خلق شي من الخير والصلاح، فحصل العالم بهما، فخالفت المجوس بهذا القول الأديان. ثم للمعتزلة مشاركة في كل ذلك فإنهم زعموا أنه كان الله تعالى ولا شيء غيره ثم حدثت إرادته من غير أن كان من الله تعالى لحدوثها إرادة أو اختيار فكان به جميع العالم، وهذا عين ما قالته المجوس إلا أنهم يسمون ذلك الحادث فكرة، والمعتزلة إرادة ولا عبرة بمخالفة الاسم عند استوائهما في المعنى، ثم جعلت المجوس لما حدث بالفكرة نصف العالم، والمعتزلة كل العالم، فشاركوا
Then whoever knows the schools and stops at what the sects of the community have of doctrines will know that the Mu'tazila are singled out from the sects of the community for sharing with the Magians in that which is characteristic of their doctrines. And the explanation of that is that the Magians said: God Almighty was one, no partner with Him, then a wicked thought occurred from Him, according to what we have related before this of their statement, so Iblis (upon him be curse) came into being from that wicked thought, and he created evils in the world, while God Almighty created good things, without God having power to create anything of evil and corruption or Iblis having power to create anything of good and righteousness, so the world came about through both of them, and thus the Magians opposed the religions with this statement. Then the Mu'tazila share in all of that, for they claimed: God Almighty existed and nothing else, then His will (irada) occurred without there being from God Almighty for its occurrence any will or choice, so the entire world came to be through it. And this is exactly what the Magians said, except that they call that occurrence a thought (fikra), and the Mu'tazila call it will (irada), and no attention is paid to the difference of name when they are equal in meaning. Then the Magians assigned to what occurred through the thought half of the world, and the Mu'tazila assigned to it the entire world, so they shared...
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage provides the doctrinal proof that the Mu'tazila are the Qadariyya by revealing their deep structural agreement with the Magians (Zoroastrians). The author first states that one who studies the sects will see that the Mu'tazila alone share specific characteristics with the Magians. He then summarizes the Magian belief: God was alone, then a wicked thought occurred from Him, from which Iblis came, and Iblis creates all evil, while God creates all good. The world results from two distinct creators, each with limited power over the other's domain. The Mu'tazila parallel this by claiming that God alone existed, then His will occurred without any prior will or choice, and through this will the entire world came to be. The crucial point is that both groups posit a secondary occurrence (thought or will) that is not under God's full control—for the Magians, the thought is an external principle; for the Mu'tazila, the will is an attribute that occurs without God's choice, implying that God's will is not completely free but emerges necessarily. Thus, both systems deny God's absolute power over evil (in the Magian case explicitly, in the Mu'tazila case implicitly by making the will a source that is not chosen). The difference that the Magians split the world between God and Iblis, while the Mu'tazila attribute all to the will, is immaterial because the underlying structure is the same: both posit a principle alongside God that limits His sovereignty. The author concludes that the Mu'tazila 'shared' (fasharakoo) in this characteristic, confirming their identification as the Qadariyya mentioned in the hadith.

Key Terms
المجوس (al-Majus/Magians)
الفكرة الرديئة (wicked thought)
إرادة (irada/will)
الشرو (evil)
الخيرات (good things)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The comparison between Mu'tazila and Magians is merely rhetorical name-calling and does not reflect actual doctrinal similarity.
Correction: The author demonstrates a substantive parallel: both groups posit a secondary principle (thought or will) that occurs without God's full control, thereby limiting His exclusive sovereignty over creation.

Checkpoint
What is the central doctrinal parallel the author draws between the Magians and the Mu'tazila?
A) Both believe in two eternal gods.
B) Both posit a secondary principle (thought or will) that occurs without God's full control and is responsible for evil or the world.
C) Both deny the existence of God's will.
D) Both affirm that God creates both good and evil directly.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila and Magians both posit a secondary principle that occurs without God's full control, undermining His exclusive sovereignty over creation—a difference in name does not change the conceptual parallel.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself explaining away moments of evil or difficulty in your life as being from 'nature', 'bad luck', or 'people's choices' without ultimately referring them back to Allah's decree? What would it cost you to truly see His hand in every event, good and bad?
?
The Magians and Mu'tazila both invented a secondary cause to protect God from evil. In what areas of your own faith have you unconsciously created 'buffer zones'—doctrines or explanations that distance Allah from parts of your life you find uncomfortable? Will you dismantle those buffers today?
?
If changing a name (from 'thought' to 'will') does not change the reality, what comfortable labels do you use to mask attitudes that contradict tawhid? Ask Allah to show you one such label in your heart right now—and confess it to Him before you move on.

The Originating Cause: Mu'tazila and Magians on Creation
Nasafi presents the Magian belief and shows the Mu'tazila share it, differing only in name and extent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi argues that the Mu'tazila share the Magian concept of an originated cause (thought/will) that brings the world into existence, and why he considers the Mu'tazila to be more extreme.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila and Magians both explain creation by an originated entity; Mu'tazila call it 'will', but they make it create the whole world.

In this passage, Nasafi draws a striking comparison between the Mu'tazila and the Magians (Zoroastrians). He argues that despite different terminology, both sects share the fundamental error of positing an originated cause (a thought or will) that arises from God and then becomes the instrument of creation. Nasafi shows that the Mu'tazila actually go further than the Magians by attributing the entire world to this originated will.

Guided Path
1
Read the Magian Belief
Read Nasafi's description of the Magian doctrine: God alone, then a wicked thought arose, Iblis originated, and he created evil while God created good.
Notice that each is powerless over the other's domain.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila Parallel
Read how the Mu'tazila claim God existed alone, then His will originated, and by it the world came to be. Note Nasafi's point: the only difference is the name.
3
Compare the Scope
Notice how Nasafi contrasts the scope: Magians attributed only half the world to the thought (evil), while Mu'tazila attribute the whole world to the will. This makes Mu'tazila worse.
They exceeded the Magians in falsehood.
4
Reflect on the Significance
Consider why Nasafi emphasizes this comparison: it shows that the Mu'tazila departure from orthodoxy is not just a minor difference but aligns them with a pre-Islamic dualist heresy.
This undermines their claim to be rational Muslims.

ثم من عرف المذاهب ووقف على ما لفرق الأمة من المقالات عرف أن المعتزلة هم المخصوصون من فرق الأمة بمشاركة المجوس فيما هو من خصائص مذاهبهم. وبيان ذلك أن المجوس قالوا كان الله تعالى واحدًا لا شريك له، ثم حدثت منه فكرة رديئة على ما حكينا قبل هذا من مقالتهم، فحدث إبليس عليه اللعنة من تلك الفكرة الرديئة فخلق هو الشرور في العالم، والله تعالى خلق الخيرات من غير أن كان الله قدرة على خلق شيء من الشر والفساد أو لإبليس قدرة على خلق شيء من الخير والصلاح، فحصل العالم بهما، فخالفت المجوس بهذا القول الأديان. ثم للمعتزلة مشاركة في كل ذلك فإنهم زعموا أنه كان الله تعالى ولا شيء غيره ثم حدثت إرادته من غير أن كان من الله تعالى لحدوثها إرادة أو اختيار فكان به جميع العالم، وهذا عين ما قالته المجوس إلا أنهم يسمون ذلك الحادث فكرة، والمعتزلة إرادة ولا عبرة بمخالفة الاسم عند استوائهما في المعنى، ثم جعلت المجوس لما حدث بالفكرة نصف العالم، والمعتزلة كل العالم، فشاركوا المجوس فيما خالفوا به جميع أهل الأديان من القول الباطل وأربوا عليهم فيه، ثم المجوس جعلت العالم بالله وبغيره ولا قدرة له على ما هو لغيره ولا قدرة لذلك الغير على ما هو له، وكذا المعتزلة جعلوا بالله وبغيره من الخالقين ولا قدرة له على ما هو لغيره ولا قدرة لغيره على ما هو له، وكذا المجوس تأبى دخول ما هو قبيح تحت قدرة الله تعالى وقصرت قدرته على المحاسن، وكذا المعتزلة ساعدوهم على هذا الأصل، وبنوا عليه جميع مذاهبهم، بل المجوس أسعد حالاً، لأنهم ما أثبتوا العالم إلا لله تعالى ولآخر، فاقتصروا على إثبات شريك واحد له، والمعتزلة أثبتوا له ما لا يحصون من الشركاء، وكذا أولئك أدخلوا جميع المحاسن تحت قدرته والمعتزلة أضافوا حسن المحاسن إلى غيره ولم يثبتوا الله تعالى على مثل تلك المحاسن قدرة على ما قررنا في مسألة خلق الأفعال، وإذا عرف هذا ظهر المراد بالاسم، والله الموفق.
Then, whoever knows the sects and pauses upon what the factions of the community have of articles knows that the Mu'tazila are the ones distinguished from the factions of the community by sharing with the Magians in what is of the characteristics of their doctrines. And the explanation of that is that the Magians said: God most high was one, no partner with Him, then a wicked thought originated from Him according to what we related before this of their statement, so Iblis (may curse be upon him) originated from that wicked thought, and he created the evils in the world, and God most high created the goods, while God had no power to create any of evil and corruption, nor did Iblis have power to create any of good and righteousness, so the world came about by the two of them, and thereby the Magians opposed the religions. Then the Mu'tazila have participation in all of that, for they claimed that God most high existed and nothing else, then His will originated without there being from God most high for its origination any will or choice, and by it all the world came into existence, and this is exactly what the Magians said, except that they call that originated thing a 'thought' and the Mu'tazila call it a 'will', and no regard is given to difference of name when they are equal in meaning. Then the Magians made, by what originated with the thought, half of the world, and the Mu'tazila [made] all of the world. Thus they participated with the Magians in what they opposed with it all the people of religions of false statement, and they exceeded them in it. Then the Magians made the world by God and by another, and He (God) has no power over what belongs to that other, nor does that other have power over what is His. Likewise the Mu'tazila made [the world] by God and by other creators, and He has no power over what belongs to that other, nor does that other have power over what is His. Likewise the Magians refuse the entry of what is ugly under the power of God most high and confined His power to good things, and likewise the Mu'tazila aided them on this principle and built upon it all their doctrines. Rather, the Magians are more fortunate, because they only affirmed the world for God most high and for another, so they confined themselves to affirming one partner for Him, while the Mu'tazila affirmed for Him partners that cannot be counted. Likewise those (Magians) included all good things under His power, and the Mu'tazila attributed the good of good things to other than Him and did not affirm for God most high power over such good things, according to what we established in the issue of the creation of acts. And when this is known, the intended meaning of the name becomes apparent. And God is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a comparative argument demonstrating that the Mu'tazila share the core heresy of the Magians (Zoroastrians) regarding divine power and the origin of evil. Nasafi begins by stating that one familiar with the sects knows that the Mu'tazila are uniquely characterized by sharing in the specifics of Magian doctrines. He then explains the Magian belief: originally God was alone, then a wicked thought arose from Him, from which Iblis emerged; Iblis created all evil, while God created only good, with each powerless over the other's domain. The Mu'tazila similarly claim that God existed alone, then His will originated without any prior will or choice, and through that originated will the entire world came to be. Nasafi notes that the only difference is nomenclature—Magians call it 'thought', Mu'tazila call it 'will'—but the meaning is identical. Moreover, the Magians attributed only half the world to the originated cause (the evil part), while the Mu'tazila attribute the whole world to the originated will, making their error greater. Nasafi then lists further analogies: both systems posit a second creator alongside God, each without power over the other's domain; both deny that evil falls under God's power, confining His power to good; the Mu'tazila even surpass the Magians by positing countless partners for God (every human agent who creates his own acts). Finally, the Mu'tazila attribute the goodness of good acts to the human agent rather than God, denying God's power over them. The passage concludes that once this is understood, the meaning of the name 'Qadariyya' (as used by the opponents of the Mu'tazila) becomes clear.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
المجوس
الفكرة
الإرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila and Magians are completely different; the comparison is merely rhetorical.
Correction: Nasafi demonstrates that they share the core error of an originated cause for creation, differing only in terminology and scope.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is the core similarity between the Mu'tazila and the Magians?
A) Both believe in two eternal gods.
B) Both deny that God creates evil.
C) Both believe that a created entity (thought or will) is the cause of the world's existence.
D) Both limit God's power over good only.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi demonstrates that the Mu'tazila not only share the Magian heresy of an originated cause for creation but surpass it by attributing the entire world to that cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult situation, do you instinctively rely on your own will and planning, forgetting that only Allah creates outcomes? How can you train yourself to see His hand in every result, not as a secondary cause but as the sole Creator?
?
The Mu'tazila claimed that God's will originated without His own choice — implicitly making that will independent. Have you ever treated your own desires as if they are ultimate, not subject to Allah's will? What would it mean for you to actively submit your will to His decree today?
?
Nasafi shows that even a difference in name (thought vs. will) can hide a shared falsehood. In your life, where might you be using 'Islamic' words to cover a concept that actually contradicts Tawhid? Be honest: is there any belief about causation, prayer, or blessing that you hold that implicitly gives power to something other than Allah?

Divine Power and Evil: Mu'tazila and Magians on the Limits of God's Power
Nasafi compares Mu'tazila and Magians on the limitation of divine power and the multiplicity of creators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi argues that the Mu'tazila follow the Magians in denying that God has power over evil, and that the Mu'tazila go even further by attributing good acts to multiple partners.

Core Idea
Both Magians and Mu'tazila confine God's power to good; Mu'tazila multiply partners beyond the Magians.

Nasafi continues his comparison by examining divine power and the origin of evil. He shows that the Magians denied God's power over evil, reserving it for Iblis, and the Mu'tazila similarly limit God's power to good acts. Moreover, the Mu'tazila assign the creation of good acts to countless human agents, making them worse than the Magians who only posited one partner.

Guided Path
1
Read the Second Creator Analogy
Nasafi states that both Magians and Mu'tazila posit a second creator. Magians have Iblis; Mu'tazila have other creators. Each is powerless over the other's domain.
Note the parallel: just as Magians said God has no power over Iblis's domain, Mu'tazila say God has no power over what humans create.
2
Notice the Denial of Evil Under God's Power
Both groups refuse to allow ugly/evil things to come from God's power, confining His power to good. Nasafi says the Mu'tazila built all their doctrines on this principle.
This is a direct challenge to the orthodox view that God is the Creator of all things, including evil.
3
Compare the Number of Partners
Magians only affirm one partner for God (Iblis). Mu'tazila affirm countless partners because every human creates his own acts. Thus Mu'tazila are more deviant.
Nasafi calls this 'affirming partners that cannot be counted'.
4
Consider the Conclusion
Nasafi ends by saying when this is known, the meaning of the name 'Qadariyya' becomes apparent. Reflect on why this comparison is more than rhetorical—it's a theological indictment.
The term Qadariyya was often used for those who denied divine predestination of evil.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Limiting God's power to good is a way to protect His goodness and avoid associating evil with Him.
Correction: Nasafi shows that this view leads to dualism and makes the Mu'tazila worse than the Magians by multiplying partners for God.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, in what way are the Mu'tazila worse than the Magians regarding the number of partners for God?
A) Magians affirm no partners.
B) Mu'tazila affirm one partner.
C) Magians affirm one partner, Mu'tazila affirm countless.
D) Both affirm countless partners.

Key Takeaway
Nasafi concludes that the Mu'tazila not only mirror the Magian limitation of divine power to good but also exceed them by affirming countless partners for God, thus earning the epithet 'Qadariyya'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you, in your heart, ever limit God's power by thinking that some evil in the world is outside His control? When you see injustice, do you silently wonder why God didn't stop it, or do you trust that it is within His power and wisdom? What would change if you consistently affirmed that nothing falls outside His power, even the things you find ugly?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you thank God for enabling it or do you feel a sense of personal achievement that subtly denies His role? Identify one good action today and consciously attribute its goodness entirely to God, not to your own ability. What resistance do you feel in doing that?
?
Nasafi says the Mu'tazila are worse than the Magians because they multiply partners for God. In your daily life, where do you have 'partners'—areas where you rely on your own strength, intellect, or others instead of God? What would it mean for you to confess that only God is the true creator of your success and failure?
